Ben walked into the coffee shop angrily after having dropped his keys in a storm drain. He walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Nick, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly he decided to walk to the front of the line and cut him. Nick was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Ben. Ben proceeded to give a slight shove to Nick. In retaliation, Nick pushed Ben. Ben saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Nick’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Nick stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Ben to leave before anyone pressed charges. Ben stared at Nick one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Nick a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “I think some caffeine would’ve helped that one.” 

Silvia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having realized that she had left her phone on the bus. She saw that there was a long line to order, so she impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Nick, the first person in line. Nick was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Silvia. Silvia proceeded to give a slight shove to Nick. In retaliation, Nick pushed Silvia. Silvia saw a muffin sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Nick’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Nick, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down his ears and shoulders. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Silvia to leave. Silvia gave Nick one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Nick a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “There was no need to worry. The baristas are trained in kung fu.” 

Silvia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having realized that she had left her phone on the bus. She walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Ben, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly she decided to walk to the front of the line and cut him. Ben was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Silvia. Silvia ignored him and proceeded to tell the barista that she would like a mocha. Ben, refusing to engage with her, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Silvia saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Ben’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Ben stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Silvia to leave before anyone pressed charges. Silvia stared at Ben one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Ben a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Im so sorry you had to experience a coffee crime.” 

Olivia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having learned that her flight to the Bahamas was cancelled due to inclement weather. She walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Jesse, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly she decided to walk to the front of the line and cut him. Jesse was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Olivia turned to Jesse and gave him a very mean look. In retaliation, Jesse pushed Olivia. Olivia saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Jesse’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Jesse stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Olivia to leave before anyone pressed charges. Olivia stared at Jesse one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Jesse a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “The nectar of the gods makes people do crazy things.”

Nick walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten a parking ticket. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Jesse, the first person in line. Jesse was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Nick. Nick ignored him and proceeded to tell the barista that he would like a mocha. In retaliation, Jesse pushed Nick. Nick saw a lemonsquare sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Jesse’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Jesse, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down his ears and shoulders. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Nick to leave. Nick gave Jesse one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Jesse a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Some people will do anything for the coffee fix.”

Ben, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down his ears and shoulders. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Jesse to leave before anyone pressed charges. Nick was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Vera. Vera ignored him and proceeded to tell the barista that she would like a coffee. Nick stared back at Vera, as though daring her with his eyes to do something.Nick refusing to engage with Vera, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Vera saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Nick’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Vera stood there gaping, cream dripping from her chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Olivia to leave before anyone pressed charges. Olivia gave Vera one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Vera a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “There was no need to worry. The baristas are trained in kung fu.” 

Ben walked into the coffee shop angrily after having dropped his keys in a storm drain. He walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Silvia, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly he decided to walk to the front of the line and cut her. Silvia was not having it that day, and she promptly stepped back in front of Ben. Ben proceeded to give a slight shove to Silvia. Silvia stared back at Ben, as though daring him with her eyes to do something.Silvia refusing to engage with Ben, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Ben saw a muffin sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Silvia’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Silvia, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Ben to leave. Ben gave Silvia one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Silvia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “The nectar of the gods makes people do crazy things.” 

Nick walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten a parking ticket. He walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Olivia, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly he decided to walk to the front of the line and cut her. Olivia was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Nick ignored her and proceeded to tell the barista that he would like a latte. In retaliation, Olivia pushed Nick. Nick saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Olivia’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Olivia stood there gaping, cream dripping from her chin. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Nick to leave. Nick stared at Olivia one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Olivia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Some people will do anything for the coffee fix.”

Ben walked into the coffee shop angrily after having dropped his keys in a storm drain. He walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Silvia, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly he decided to walk to the front of the line and cut her. Silvia was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Ben proceeded to give a slight shove to Silvia. Silvia stared back at Ben, as though daring him with her eyes to do something.Silvia refusing to engage with Ben, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Ben saw a lemonsquare sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Silvia’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Silvia, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Ben to leave before anyone pressed charges. Ben stared at Silvia one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Silvia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Some people will do anything for the coffee fix.” 

Ben walked into the coffee shop angrily after having dropped his keys in a storm drain. He walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Silvia, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly he decided to walk to the front of the line and cut her. Silvia was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Ben proceeded to give a slight shove to Silvia. Silvia, refusing to engage with him, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Ben saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Silvia’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Silvia stood there gaping, cream dripping from her chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Ben to leave before anyone pressed charges. Ben gave Silvia one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Silvia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “The nectar of the gods makes people do crazy things.” 

Nick walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten a parking ticket. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Jesse, the first person in line. Jesse was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Nick. Nick ignored him and proceeded to tell the barista that he would like a latte. In retaliation, Jesse pushed Nick. Nick saw a cake sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Jesse’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Jesse, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down his ears and shoulders. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Nick to leave before anyone pressed charges. Nick gave Jesse one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Jesse a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “I think some caffeine would’ve helped that one.” 

Olivia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having learned that her flight to the Bahamas was cancelled due to inclement weather. She walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Vera, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly she decided to walk to the front of the line and cut her. Vera was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Olivia ignored her and proceeded to tell the barista that she would like a latte. Vera stared back at Olivia, as though daring her with her eyes to do something.Vera refusing to engage with Olivia, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Olivia saw a lemonsquare sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Vera’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Vera, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Olivia to leave before anyone pressed charges. Olivia stared at Vera one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Vera a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “I think some caffeine would’ve helped that one.” 

Nick walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten a parking ticket. He walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Silvia, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly he decided to walk to the front of the line and cut her. Silvia was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Nick ignored her and proceeded to tell the barista that he would like a coffee. Silvia stared back at Nick, as though daring him with her eyes to do something.Silvia refusing to engage with Nick, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Nick saw a muffin sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Silvia’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Silvia, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Nick to leave. Nick gave Silvia one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Silvia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “There was no need to worry. The baristas are trained in kung fu.”

Ben was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Jesse proceeded to give a slight shove to Ben. In retaliation, Ben pushed Jesse. Jesse saw a cake sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Ben’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Ben, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down his ears and shoulders. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Jesse to leave before anyone pressed charges. Nick walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten a parking ticket. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Ben, the first person in line. Ben was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Nick. Nick turned to Ben and gave him a very mean look. In retaliation, Ben pushed Nick. Nick saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Ben’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Ben stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Nick to leave. Nick gave Ben one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Ben a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Some people will do anything for the coffee fix.”

Everyone in line gasped. Olivia stood there gaping, cream dripping from her chin. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Jesse to leave. Jesse gave Olivia one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Olivia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “The nectar of the gods makes people do crazy things.” 

Vera walked into the coffee shop angrily after having found her calculus problem set ripped to shreds in her dog’s cage. She saw that there was a long line to order, so she impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Olivia, the first person in line. Olivia was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Vera ignored her and proceeded to tell the barista that she would like a latte. In retaliation, Olivia pushed Vera. Vera saw a lemonsquare sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Olivia’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Olivia, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Vera to leave. Vera stared at Olivia one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Olivia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “The nectar of the gods makes people do crazy things.”

Olivia was not having it that day, and she promptly stepped back in front of Vera. Vera turned to Olivia and gave her a very mean look. Olivia stared back at Vera, as though daring her with her eyes to do something.Olivia refusing to engage with Vera, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Vera saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Olivia’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Olivia stood there gaping, cream dripping from her chin. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Vera to leave. Vera stared at Olivia one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Olivia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “The nectar of the gods makes people do crazy things.” 

Nick walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten a parking ticket. He walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Vera, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly he decided to walk to the front of the line and cut her. Vera was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Nick turned to Vera and gave her a very mean look. Vera, refusing to engage with him, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Nick saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Vera’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Vera stood there gaping, cream dripping from her chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Nick to leave before anyone pressed charges. Nick stared at Vera one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Vera a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “There was no need to worry. The baristas are trained in kung fu.” 

Olivia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having learned that her flight to the Bahamas was cancelled due to inclement weather. She saw that there was a long line to order, so she impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Nick, the first person in line. Nick was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Olivia. Olivia ignored him and proceeded to tell the barista that she would like a latte. Nick, refusing to engage with her, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Olivia saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Nick’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Nick stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Olivia to leave before anyone pressed charges. Olivia stared at Nick one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Nick a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “I think some caffeine would’ve helped that one.” 

Nick walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten a parking ticket. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Jesse, the first person in line. Jesse was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Nick. Nick turned to Jesse and gave him a very mean look. In retaliation, Jesse pushed Nick. Nick saw a cookie sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Jesse’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Jesse, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down his ears and shoulders. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Nick to leave. Nick gave Jesse one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Jesse a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “There was no need to worry. The baristas are trained in kung fu.” 

Jesse walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten into a fight with his mom. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Vera, the first person in line. Vera was not having it that day, and she promptly stepped back in front of Jesse. Jesse proceeded to give a slight shove to Vera. Vera, refusing to engage with him, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Jesse saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Vera’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Vera stood there gaping, cream dripping from her chin. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Jesse to leave. Ben walked into the coffee shop angrily after having dropped his keys in a storm drain. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Silvia, the first person in line. Silvia was not having it that day, and she promptly stepped back in front of Ben. Ben ignored her and proceeded to tell the barista that he would like a mocha. Silvia stared back at Ben, as though daring him with her eyes to do something.Silvia refusing to engage with Ben, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Ben saw a muffin sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Silvia’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Silvia, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Ben to leave before anyone pressed charges. Ben gave Silvia one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Silvia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “The nectar of the gods makes people do crazy things.” 

Vera walked into the coffee shop angrily after having found her calculus problem set ripped to shreds in her dog’s cage. She saw that there was a long line to order, so she impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Ben, the first person in line. Ben was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Vera proceeded to give a slight shove to Ben. In retaliation, Ben pushed Vera. Vera saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Ben’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Ben stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Vera to leave. Vera gave Ben one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Ben a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Im so sorry you had to experience a coffee crime.”

Nick walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten a parking ticket. He walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Ben, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly he decided to walk to the front of the line and cut him. Ben was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Nick ignored him and proceeded to tell the barista that he would like a coffee. Ben stared back at Nick, as though daring him with his eyes to do something.Ben refusing to engage with Nick, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Nick saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Ben’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Ben stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Nick to leave before anyone pressed charges. Nick stared at Ben one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Ben a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “I think some caffeine would’ve helped that one.” 

Silvia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having realized that she had left her phone on the bus. She saw that there was a long line to order, so she impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Vera, the first person in line. Vera was not having it that day, and she promptly stepped back in front of Silvia. Silvia turned to Vera and gave her a very mean look. Vera, refusing to engage with her, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Silvia saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Vera’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Vera stood there gaping, cream dripping from her chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Silvia to leave before anyone pressed charges. Silvia stared at Vera one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Vera a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Its not everyday you meet a coffee criminal.” 

Nick walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten a parking ticket. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Jesse, the first person in line. Jesse was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Nick. Nick turned to Jesse and gave him a very mean look. Jesse stared back at Nick, as though daring him with his eyes to do something.Jesse refusing to engage with Nick, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Nick saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Jesse’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Jesse stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Nick to leave. Nick gave Jesse one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Jesse a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “I think some caffeine would’ve helped that one.” 

Nick walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten a parking ticket. He walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Jesse, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly he decided to walk to the front of the line and cut him. Jesse was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Nick turned to Jesse and gave him a very mean look. In retaliation, Jesse pushed Nick. Nick saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Jesse’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Jesse stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Nick to leave before anyone pressed charges. Nick gave Jesse one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Jesse a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “I think some caffeine would’ve helped that one.” 

Silvia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having realized that she had left her phone on the bus. She walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Nick, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly she decided to walk to the front of the line and cut him. Nick was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Silvia. Silvia proceeded to give a slight shove to Nick. Nick, refusing to engage with her, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Silvia saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Nick’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Nick stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Silvia to leave before anyone pressed charges. Silvia stared at Nick one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Nick a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Im so sorry you had to experience a coffee crime.” 

Jesse walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten into a fight with his mom. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Vera, the first person in line. Vera was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Jesse ignored her and proceeded to tell the barista that he would like a coffee. Vera stared back at Jesse, as though daring him with her eyes to do something.Vera refusing to engage with Jesse, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Jesse saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Vera’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Vera stood there gaping, cream dripping from her chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Jesse to leave before anyone pressed charges. Jesse gave Vera one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Vera a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “There was no need to worry. The baristas are trained in kung fu.” 

Silvia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having realized that she had left her phone on the bus. She saw that there was a long line to order, so she impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Jesse, the first person in line. Jesse was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Silvia. Silvia ignored him and proceeded to tell the barista that she would like a coffee. Jesse stared back at Silvia, as though daring her with his eyes to do something.Jesse refusing to engage with Silvia, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Silvia saw a muffin sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Jesse’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Jesse, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down his ears and shoulders. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Silvia to leave. Silvia stared at Jesse one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Jesse a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Some people will do anything for the coffee fix.” 

Ben walked into the coffee shop angrily after having dropped his keys in a storm drain. He walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Jesse, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly he decided to walk to the front of the line and cut him. Jesse was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Ben. Ben proceeded to give a slight shove to Jesse. In retaliation, Jesse pushed Ben. Ben saw a lemonsquare sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Jesse’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Jesse, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down his ears and shoulders. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Ben to leave before anyone pressed charges. Ben gave Jesse one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Jesse a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Im so sorry you had to experience a coffee crime.”

Vera walked into the coffee shop angrily after having found her calculus problem set ripped to shreds in her dog’s cage. She saw that there was a long line to order, so she impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Silvia, the first person in line. Silvia was not having it that day, and she promptly stepped back in front of Vera. Vera turned to Silvia and gave her a very mean look. Silvia, refusing to engage with her, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Vera saw a cookie sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Silvia’s head. Olivia stared back at Vera, as though daring her with her eyes to do something.Olivia refusing to engage with Vera, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Vera saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Olivia’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Olivia stood there gaping, cream dripping from her chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Vera to leave before anyone pressed charges. Vera stared at Olivia one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Olivia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “There was no need to worry. The baristas are trained in kung fu.” 

Nick walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten a parking ticket. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Ben, the first person in line. Ben was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Nick. Nick turned to Ben and gave him a very mean look. Ben, refusing to engage with him, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Nick saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Ben’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Ben stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Nick to leave before anyone pressed charges. Nick stared at Ben one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Ben a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “I think some caffeine would’ve helped that one.” 

Silvia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having realized that she had left her phone on the bus. She walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Vera, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly she decided to walk to the front of the line and cut her. Vera was not having it that day, and she promptly stepped back in front of Silvia. Silvia ignored her and proceeded to tell the barista that she would like a latte. Vera, refusing to engage with her, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Silvia saw a cookie sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Vera’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Vera, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Silvia to leave. Silvia gave Vera one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Vera a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Im so sorry you had to experience a coffee crime.”

Olivia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having learned that her flight to the Bahamas was cancelled due to inclement weather. She walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Ben, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly she decided to walk to the front of the line and cut him. Ben was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Olivia proceeded to give a slight shove to Ben. In retaliation, Ben pushed Olivia. Olivia saw a lemonsquare sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Ben’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Ben, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down his ears and shoulders. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Olivia to leave before anyone pressed charges. Olivia stared at Ben one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. Silvia was not having it that day, and she promptly stepped back in front of Jesse. Jesse proceeded to give a slight shove to Silvia. Silvia stared back at Jesse, as though daring him with her eyes to do something.Silvia refusing to engage with Jesse, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Jesse saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Silvia’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Silvia stood there gaping, cream dripping from her chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Jesse to leave before anyone pressed charges. Jesse stared at Silvia one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Silvia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “There was no need to worry. The baristas are trained in kung fu.” 

Vera walked into the coffee shop angrily after having found her calculus problem set ripped to shreds in her dog’s cage. She saw that there was a long line to order, so she impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Olivia, the first person in line. Olivia was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Vera turned to Olivia and gave her a very mean look. Olivia, refusing to engage with her, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Vera saw a cake sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Olivia’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Olivia, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Vera to leave. Vera stared at Olivia one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Olivia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “The nectar of the gods makes people do crazy things.” 

Ben walked into the coffee shop angrily after having dropped his keys in a storm drain. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Nick, the first person in line. Nick was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Ben proceeded to give a slight shove to Nick. Nick stared back at Ben, as though daring him with his eyes to do something.Nick refusing to engage with Ben, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Ben saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Nick’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Nick stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Ben to leave before anyone pressed charges. Ben stared at Nick one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Nick a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Im so sorry you had to experience a coffee crime.” 

Vera walked into the coffee shop angrily after having found her calculus problem set ripped to shreds in her dog’s cage. She saw that there was a long line to order, so she impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Ben, the first person in line. Ben was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Vera. Vera ignored him and proceeded to tell the barista that she would like a mocha. Ben, refusing to engage with her, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Vera saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Ben’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Ben stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Vera to leave before anyone pressed charges. Vera stared at Ben one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Ben a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “The nectar of the gods makes people do crazy things.” 

Olivia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having learned that her flight to the Bahamas was cancelled due to inclement weather. She walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Nick, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly she decided to walk to the front of the line and cut him. Nick was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Olivia. Olivia proceeded to give a slight shove to Nick. Nick, refusing to engage with her, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Olivia saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Nick’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Nick stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Olivia to leave before anyone pressed charges. Olivia stared at Nick one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Nick a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “There was no need to worry. The baristas are trained in kung fu.” 

Olivia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having learned that her flight to the Bahamas was cancelled due to inclement weather. She saw that there was a long line to order, so she impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Vera, the first person in line. Vera was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Olivia ignored her and proceeded to tell the barista that she would like a mocha. Vera, refusing to engage with her, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Olivia saw a cake sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Vera’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Vera, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Olivia to leave before anyone pressed charges. Olivia stared at Vera one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Vera a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Its not everyday you meet a coffee criminal.” 

Silvia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having realized that she had left her phone on the bus. She walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Jesse, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly she decided to walk to the front of the line and cut him. Jesse was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Silvia. Silvia ignored him and proceeded to tell the barista that she would like a coffee. In retaliation, Jesse pushed Silvia. Silvia saw a cake sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Jesse’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Jesse, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down his ears and shoulders. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Silvia to leave. Silvia gave Jesse one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Jesse a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Some people will do anything for the coffee fix.” 

Jesse walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten into a fight with his mom. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Vera, the first person in line. Vera was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Jesse proceeded to give a slight shove to Vera. Vera, refusing to engage with him, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Jesse saw a lemonsquare sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Vera’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Vera, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Jesse to leave before anyone pressed charges. Jesse gave Vera one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Vera a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “I think some caffeine would’ve helped that one.”

Vera stared back at Ben, as though daring him with her eyes to do something.Vera refusing to engage with Ben, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Ben saw a lemonsquare sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Vera’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Vera, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Ben to leave before anyone pressed charges. Ben stared at Vera one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Vera a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “The nectar of the gods makes people do crazy things.” 

Jesse walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten into a fight with his mom. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Silvia, the first person in line. Silvia was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Jesse turned to Silvia and gave her a very mean look. In retaliation, Silvia pushed Jesse. Jesse saw a muffin sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Silvia’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Silvia, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Jesse to leave before anyone pressed charges. Jesse stared at Silvia one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Silvia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “There was no need to worry. The baristas are trained in kung fu.”

Jesse walked into the coffee shop angrily after having gotten into a fight with his mom. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Nick, the first person in line. Nick was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Jesse ignored him and proceeded to tell the barista that he would like a mocha. Nick, refusing to engage with him, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Jesse saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Nick’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Nick stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Jesse to leave before anyone pressed charges. Jesse stared at Nick one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Nick a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “Some people will do anything for the coffee fix.”

Vera walked into the coffee shop angrily after having found her calculus problem set ripped to shreds in her dog’s cage. She saw that there was a long line to order, so she impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Olivia, the first person in line. Olivia was not having it that day, and she promptly stepped back in front of Vera. Vera ignored her and proceeded to tell the barista that she would like a coffee. Olivia, refusing to engage with her, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Vera saw a lemonsquare sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Olivia’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Olivia, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista ran out from behind the counter and ordered Vera to leave. Vera gave Olivia one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Olivia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “There was no need to worry. The baristas are trained in kung fu.”

Ben gave Silvia one last stare, turned, and ran out yelling, “Juice is better, anyway!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Silvia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “The nectar of the gods makes people do crazy things.” 

Olivia walked into the coffee shop angrily after having learned that her flight to the Bahamas was cancelled due to inclement weather. She walked to the back of the line and stood impatiently, watching the first person in line, Silvia, staring idly at the menu. Suddenly she decided to walk to the front of the line and cut her. Silvia was astonished and said, “Excuse me?!’ Olivia ignored her and proceeded to tell the barista that she would like a mocha. Silvia stared back at Olivia, as though daring her with her eyes to do something.Silvia refusing to engage with Olivia, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Olivia saw a lemonsquare sitting like ammo next to the cash register, snatched it, and crumbled it above Silvia’s head. Everyone in line gasped. Silvia, in shock, didn’t move as crumbs tumbled down her ears and shoulders. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and he ordered Olivia to leave before anyone pressed charges. Olivia stared at Silvia one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Silvia a bunch of napkins and gave her a free drink out of sympathy, saying “The nectar of the gods makes people do crazy things.” 

Ben walked into the coffee shop angrily after having dropped his keys in a storm drain. He saw that there was a long line to order, so he impatiently walked to the front of the line and cut Jesse, the first person in line. Jesse was not having it that day, and he promptly stepped back in front of Ben. Ben proceeded to give a slight shove to Jesse. Jesse, refusing to engage with him, turned to the barista and said, ‘I was first in line!” Ben saw a small cup of cream on the counter, picked it up, and splashed it in Jesse’s face. Everyone in line gasped. Jesse stood there gaping, cream dripping from his chin. The barista called over to a policeman standing in line, and she ordered Ben to leave before anyone pressed charges. Ben stared at Jesse one last time, then stormed out of the coffee shop, yelling, “I hate coffee!” Everyone at the coffee shop turned to each other wondering if that had really just happened. The barista handed Jesse a bunch of napkins and gave him a free drink out of sympathy, saying “The nectar of the gods makes people do crazy things.”

Mariko walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. She found an empty chair next to Sarah. "Oh hi there Mariko!" said Sarah. "I'm glad you could make it Sarah!" Mariko replied. Olivia, who was the emcee for tonight, walked to the front of the room and introduced the first poet, Julian. Julian stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that he had written: "I wandered lonely as a cloud that floats on high o'er vales and hills, when all at once I saw a crowd, A host, of golden daffodils." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Mariko had also written a poem, but decided that she wasn't in the mood to share it today. After all the poets had performed, Mariko and Sarah said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Mariko made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Pradeep walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. He walked to the counter and decided on a coffee. He found an empty chair next to Mariko. "I'm glad you could make it Pradeep!" said Mariko. "Hey Mariko!" Pradeep replied. Olivia, who was the emcee for tonight, walked to the front of the room and introduced the first poet, Julian. Julian stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that he had written: "I wandered lonely as a cloud that floats on high o'er vales and hills, when all at once I saw a crowd, A host, of golden daffodils." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Pradeep then took at turn at the microphone. "Twas brillig, and the slithy toves did gyre and gimble in the wabe: all mimsy were the borogoves, and the mome raths outgrab." When he sat back down, Mariko said that she loved the poem. After all the poets had performed, Pradeep and Mariko said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Pradeep made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Will walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. He walked to the counter and decided on a tea. He found an empty chair next to Sarah. "Oh hi there Will!" said Sarah. "Great to see you Sarah!" Will replied. Pradeep stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that he had written: "Twas brillig, and the slithy toves did gyre and gimble in the wabe: all mimsy were the borogoves, and the mome raths outgrab." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Will then took at turn at the microphone. "Love at the lips was touch, as sweet as I could bear, and once that seemed too much, I lived on air." When he sat back down, Sarah said that she loved the poem. After all the poets had performed, Will and Sarah said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. On the way out, Will ordered a cake to take home. The barista took one from the display case and wrapped it up to go. Will made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Mariko walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. She found an empty chair next to Sarah. "Oh hi there Mariko!" said Sarah. "I'm glad you could make it Sarah!" Mariko replied. Olivia stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that she had written: "For I have known them all already, known them all: have known the evenings, mornings, afternoons; I have measured out my life with coffee spoons." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Mariko then took at turn at the microphone. "He was my North, my South, my East and my West, my working week and my Sunday rest, my noon, my midnight, my talk, my song; I thought that love would last forever, I was wrong." When she sat back down, Sarah said that she loved the poem. After all the poets had performed, Mariko and Sarah said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Mariko made a mental note to come back again next week.

"Twas brillig, and the slithy toves did gyre and gimble in the wabe: all mimsy were the borogoves, and the mome raths outgrab." When he sat back down, Mariko said that she loved the poem. After all the poets had performed, Pradeep and Mariko said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Pradeep made a mental note to come back again next week.

After all the poets had performed, Sarah and Will said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. On the way out, Sarah ordered a cake to take home. The barista took one from the display case and wrapped it up to go. Sarah made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Julian walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. He found an empty chair next to Pradeep. "Hey Julian!" said Pradeep. "It's been too long Pradeep!" Julian replied. The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Julian then took at turn at the microphone. "I wandered lonely as a cloud that floats on high o'er vales and hills, when all at once I saw a crowd, A host, of golden daffodils." When he sat back down, Pradeep said that he loved the poem. After all the poets had performed, Julian and Pradeep said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Julian made a mental note to come back again next week.

Pradeep stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that he had written: "Twas brillig, and the slithy toves did gyre and gimble in the wabe: all mimsy were the borogoves, and the mome raths outgrab." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Sarah had also written a poem, but decided that she wasn't in the mood to share it today. After all the poets had performed, Sarah and Mariko said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Sarah made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Olivia walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. She walked to the counter and decided on a latte. But after hearing how expensive it was, she canceled the order. She found an empty chair next to Will. "Great to see you Olivia!" said Will. "Howdy Will!" Olivia replied. Pradeep stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that he had written: "Twas brillig, and the slithy toves did gyre and gimble in the wabe: all mimsy were the borogoves, and the mome raths outgrab." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Olivia then took at turn at the microphone. "For I have known them all already, known them all: have known the evenings, mornings, afternoons; I have measured out my life with coffee spoons." When she sat back down, Will said that he loved the poem. After all the poets had performed, Olivia and Will said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. On the way out, Olivia ordered a mousse to take home. The barista took one from the refrigerator and wrapped it up to go. Olivia made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Sarah walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. She found an empty chair next to Pradeep. "Hey Sarah!" said Pradeep. "Oh hi there Pradeep!" Sarah replied. Will stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that he had written: "Love at the lips was touch, as sweet as I could bear, and once that seemed too much, I lived on air." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Sarah had also written a poem, but decided that she wasn't in the mood to share it today. After all the poets had performed, Sarah and Pradeep said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. On the way out, Sarah ordered a sorbet to take home. Julian walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. He found an empty chair next to Will. "Great to see you Julian!" said Will. "It's been too long Will!" Julian replied. Olivia stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that she had written: "For I have known them all already, known them all: have known the evenings, mornings, afternoons; I have measured out my life with coffee spoons." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Julian then took at turn at the microphone. "I wandered lonely as a cloud that floats on high o'er vales and hills, when all at once I saw a crowd, A host, of golden daffodils." When he sat back down, Will said that he loved the poem. After all the poets had performed, Julian and Will said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Julian made a mental note to come back again next week.

Julian stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that he had written: "I wandered lonely as a cloud that floats on high o'er vales and hills, when all at once I saw a crowd, A host, of golden daffodils." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Mariko had also written a poem, but decided that she wasn't in the mood to share it today. After all the poets had performed, Mariko and Olivia said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Mariko made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Pradeep walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. He walked to the counter and decided on a coffee. He found an empty chair next to Sarah. "Oh hi there Pradeep!" said Sarah. "Hey Sarah!" Pradeep replied. Olivia stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that she had written: "For I have known them all already, known them all: have known the evenings, mornings, afternoons; I have measured out my life with coffee spoons." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Pradeep then took at turn at the microphone. "Twas brillig, and the slithy toves did gyre and gimble in the wabe: all mimsy were the borogoves, and the mome raths outgrab." When he sat back down, Sarah said that she loved the poem. After all the poets had performed, Pradeep and Sarah said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Pradeep made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Julian walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. He walked to the counter and decided on a coffee. He found an empty chair next to Pradeep. "Hey Julian!" said Pradeep. "It's been too long Pradeep!" Julian replied. Olivia, who was the emcee for tonight, walked to the front of the room and introduced the first poet, Will. Will stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that he had written: "Love at the lips was touch, as sweet as I could bear, and once that seemed too much, I lived on air." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Julian then took at turn at the microphone. "I wandered lonely as a cloud that floats on high o'er vales and hills, when all at once I saw a crowd, A host, of golden daffodils." When he sat back down, Pradeep said that he loved the poem. After all the poets had performed, Julian and Pradeep said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Julian made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Pradeep walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. He walked to the counter and decided on a latte. He found an empty chair next to Mariko. "I'm glad you could make it Pradeep!" said Mariko. "Hey Mariko!" Pradeep replied. Sarah, who was the emcee for tonight, walked to the front of the room and introduced the first poet, Will. Will stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that he had written: "Love at the lips was touch, as sweet as I could bear, and once that seemed too much, I lived on air." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Pradeep then took at turn at the microphone. "Twas brillig, and the slithy toves did gyre and gimble in the wabe: all mimsy were the borogoves, and the mome raths outgrab." When he sat back down, Mariko said that she loved the poem. After all the poets had performed, Pradeep and Mariko said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. On the way out, Pradeep ordered a cake to take home. The barista took one from the display case and wrapped it up to go. Pradeep made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Olivia walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. She walked to the counter and decided on a tea. She found an empty chair next to Mariko. "I'm glad you could make it Olivia!" said Mariko. "Howdy Mariko!" Olivia replied. Sarah stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that she had written: "You may write me down in history with your bitter, twisted lies, you may trod me in the very dirt but still, like dust, I'll rise." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Olivia then took at turn at the microphone. "For I have known them all already, known them all: have known the evenings, mornings, afternoons; I have measured out my life with coffee spoons." When she sat back down, Mariko said that she loved the poem. After all the poets had performed, Olivia and Mariko said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. On the way out, Olivia ordered a mousse to take home. The barista took one from the refrigerator and wrapped it up to go. Olivia made a mental note to come back again next week.

The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Olivia had also written a poem, but decided that she wasn't in the mood to share it today. After all the poets had performed, Olivia and Will said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. On the way out, Olivia ordered a mousse to take home. The barista took one from the refrigerator and wrapped it up to go. Olivia made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Pradeep walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. He walked to the counter and decided on a tea. He found an empty chair next to Olivia. "Howdy Pradeep!" said Olivia. "Hey Olivia!" Pradeep replied. Julian, who was the emcee for tonight, walked to the front of the room and introduced the first poet, Mariko. Mariko stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that she had written: "He was my North, my South, my East and my West, my working week and my Sunday rest, my noon, my midnight, my talk, my song; I thought that love would last forever, I was wrong." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Pradeep then took at turn at the microphone. "Twas brillig, and the slithy toves did gyre and gimble in the wabe: all mimsy were the borogoves, and the mome raths outgrab." When he sat back down, Olivia said that she loved the poem. After all the poets had performed, Pradeep and Olivia said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Pradeep made a mental note to come back again next week.

Mariko walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. She walked to the counter and decided on a tea. She found an empty chair next to Julian. "It's been too long Mariko!" said Julian. "I'm glad you could make it Julian!" Mariko replied. Will stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that he had written: "Love at the lips was touch, as sweet as I could bear, and once that seemed too much, I lived on air." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Mariko had also written a poem, but decided that she wasn't in the mood to share it today. After all the poets had performed, Mariko and Julian said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Mariko made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Will walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. He walked to the counter and decided on a tea. He found an empty chair next to Pradeep. "Hey Will!" said Pradeep. "Great to see you Pradeep!" Will replied. Mariko, who was the emcee for tonight, walked to the front of the room and introduced the first poet, Sarah. Sarah stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that she had written: "You may write me down in history with your bitter, twisted lies, you may trod me in the very dirt but still, like dust, I'll rise." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Will had also written a poem, but decided that he wasn't in the mood to share it today. After all the poets had performed, Will and Pradeep said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Will made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Sarah walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. She walked to the counter and decided on a latte. But after hearing how expensive it was, she canceled the order. She found an empty chair next to Olivia. "Howdy Sarah!" said Olivia. "Oh hi there Olivia!" Sarah replied. Pradeep stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that he had written: "Twas brillig, and the slithy toves did gyre and gimble in the wabe: all mimsy were the borogoves, and the mome raths outgrab." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Sarah had also written a poem, but decided that she wasn't in the mood to share it today. After all the poets had performed, Sarah and Olivia said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Sarah made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Olivia walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. She walked to the counter and decided on a tea. She found an empty chair next to Pradeep. "Hey Olivia!" said Pradeep. "Howdy Pradeep!" Olivia replied. Sarah, who was the emcee for tonight, walked to the front of the room and introduced the first poet, Mariko. Mariko stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that she had written: "He was my North, my South, my East and my West, my working week and my Sunday rest, my noon, my midnight, my talk, my song; I thought that love would last forever, I was wrong." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Olivia had also written a poem, but decided that she wasn't in the mood to share it today. After all the poets had performed, Olivia and Pradeep said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. On the way out, Olivia ordered a mousse to take home. The barista took one from the refrigerator and wrapped it up to go. Olivia made a mental note to come back again next week. 

Sarah walked into the coffee shop on poetry night. She walked to the counter and decided on a tea. She found an empty chair next to Will. "Great to see you Sarah!" said Will. "Oh hi there Will!" Sarah replied. Julian, who was the emcee for tonight, walked to the front of the room and introduced the first poet, Olivia. Olivia stepped up to the microphone and read the poem that she had written: "For I have known them all already, known them all: have known the evenings, mornings, afternoons; I have measured out my life with coffee spoons." The crowd snapped their fingers politely. Sarah had also written a poem, but decided that she wasn't in the mood to share it today. After all the poets had performed, Sarah and Will said their goodbyes and walked toward the door. Sarah made a mental note to come back again next week.
